**PREFACE **

It gives me great pleasure to present to the world of scholars the present edition of the ┼Ъ┼Ъ─Бrad─лy─Бkhyan─Бmam─Бl─Б of Harс╣гak─лrti shortly after my edition of the Anek─Бrthatilaka of Mah─лpa published in the same Series in 1947. The work of preparing a critical edition of the ┼Ъ─Бrad─лy─Бkhyan─Бmam─Бl─Б was entrusted to me in the year 1950 by Dr. S. M. KATRE, Director of the Deccan College Research Institute, Poona, for being included in the InstituteтАЩs Series called the тАШContributory Studies towards A Dictionary of Sanskrit on Historical PrinciplesтАЩ in general and the тАШSources of Indo-Aryan LexicographyтАЩ in particular. I started my work on the critical edition of the ┼ЪN soon after it was entrusted to me by procuring five manuscripts of the work-four from the Government Manuscripts Library at the Bhandarkar Oriental Research Institute, Poona and one from the Manuscripts Library of the Deccan College Research Institute and having worked at it at different intervals, submitted to the Institute my press-copy early in January 1951. I am glad that the work is now available in print without any delay.

Before concluding the preface it is my pleasant duty to acknowledge with gratitude the help I received from several persons in bringing out this volume. In this connection my thanks are due to Dr. S. M. KATRE, for giving me an opportunity to edit for the second time a lexicographical work in the тАШSources of Indo-Aryan LexicographyтАЩ Series undertaken by the Institute. I am also thankful to Prof. P. K. GODE, M.A., Curator, Bhandarkar Oriental Research Institute, Poona, for the loan of the four manuscripts of the ┼ЪN from the Government Manuscripts Library, and to Dr. R. G. HARSHE, D.LITT. (Paris), Registrar, Deccan College Research Institute, for allowing me the use of one manuscript of the work from the InstituteтАЩs collection of manuscripts. I must also thank Miss Suman N. DHAVALE, G.A., but for whose help in the irksome task of preparing the glossary appended to the text, it would not have been possible for me to complete my press-copy so early. Lastly, I have to put on record my sincere thanks to Pt. K. V. K. SHARMA, Vy─Бkaraс╣Зavidv─Бn, my colleague in the Sanskrit Dictionary Department, for helping me in correcting the proofs with valuable suggestions at times and to Mr. S. R. PARANJPE, the enthusiastic Manager of the Poona University Press for the prompt and efficient printing of this work. The Samartha Bharat Press, Poona, also deserves my thanks for the printing of the preliminary portion and the glossary.

D. C. P. and R. Institute,
POONA, 6
M. M. PATKAR
7th April 1951

**INTRODUCTION **

The ┼Ъ─Бrad─лy─Бkhyan─Бmam─Бl─Б or ┼Ъ─Бrad─лy─Бbhidh─Бnam─Бl─Б , as it is sometimes called, is a glossary of synonymous words and is divided into three k─Бс╣Зс╕Нas, each of which is again sub-divided into different vargas. Thus the first k─Бс╣Зс╕Нa is divided into 1 devavarga, 2 vyomavarga and 3 dhar─Бvarga; the second is divided into 1 aс╣Еgavarga, 2 samyog─Бdivarga, 3 saс╣Бg─лtavarga and 4 paс╣Зс╕Нitavarga. The last k─Бс╣Зс╕Нais divided into 1 brahmavarga, 2 r─Бjavarga, 3 vai┼Ыyavarga, 4 ┼Ы┼лdravarga, and 5 saс╣Бk─лrс╣Зavarga. The whole work consists of about 465 stanzas.

The Author

The Author of the work belonged to a Jain sect, his name being Harс╣гak─лrti. He was a High Priest belonging to the N─Бgapur─лyatap─Бgaccha branch of the Jain priests,┬╣and was the pupil of Candrak─лrti, who was highly honoured by emperor Jehangir of Delhi, who ruled from A.D. 1545 to 1553. In his pra┼Ыasti to the Dh─Бtup─Бс╣нhataraс╣Еgiс╣З─л, Harс╣гak─лrti gives the following list of persons in his line who were honoured by royal personages:тАФ

1.Jaya┼Ыekhara, honoured by Hamm─лra (1301-1365 A.D.)
2. Vajrasena, honoured by All─Бvadi┬▓(1295-1316 A.D.)
3. Ratna┼Ыekhara, honoured by Perojshah (1351-1388 A.D.)
4. Haс╣Бsak─лrti, honoured by Sikandara Shab, probably Sikandar Shah Lodi^(3)(1488-1518)
5. ─Аnandar─Бya, obtained the title R─Бya from Humayun (1530-1540)
6. Candrak─лrti, teacher of Harс╣гak─лrti, who wrote the present work. Candrakirti was honoured by Shah Salem or Jehangir (1545-1553)
7. Padmasundaragaс╣Зi, honoured by Akbar (1556-1605)
8. Pacca, honoured by a Hindu king named M─Бladeva, who was the ruler of Yodhapura i.e. modern Jodhpur. R. G. BHANDARKAR states that M─Бladeva was a prince of the R─Бthod family which ruled at Jodhpur from A.D. 1532 to 1583.тБ┤

Harс╣гak─лrtiтАЩs Works and Date

Harс╣гak─лrti was a versatile writer and wrote on different subjects such as grammar, medicine, astrology and so on. Most of his writing

Scholars differ in their opinion concerning the date of Harс╣гak─лrti. According to WEBER┬╣┬╣ Harс╣гak─лrti, the author of the ┼Ъ─Бrad─лy─Бkhyan─Бmam─Бl─Б, lived towards тАШthe end of the sixteenth centuryтАЩ. BELVALKAR┬╣┬▓ assigns the date тАШcirca 1560 A.D.тАЩ to Harс╣гak─лrti, probably relying on the fact that Harс╣гak─лrti was a pupil of Candrak─лrti who was honoured by Salimshah alias Jehangir who ruled from A.D. 1545 to 1553. Judging, however, from the works ascribed to Harс╣гak─лrti in the above list we are inclined to assign Harс╣гak─лrti a period тАШbetween A.D. 1575 to 1625тАЩ for his literary activity. From the list of works ascribed to Harс╣гak─лrti we come to know that he composed the Bс╣Ыhacch─Бntistotraс╣н─лk─Б in saс╣Бvat 1655 i.e. A.D. 1599, and the Seс╣нaniс╣нk─Бrik─Бvivaraс╣Зa in saс╣Бvat 1669 or A.D. 1613.

тАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФтАФ

It is also stated that a manuscript of Ny─Бy─Бvat─Бra was copied for him in saс╣Бvat 1635 i.e. A.D. 1579.

It will be seen from the foregoing remarks that Harс╣гak─лrti must have already commenced his literary studies in A.D. 1579 when he got a manuscript of Ny─Бy─Бvat─Бra copied for his use. It is also evident that his literary activity continued at least up to A D. 1613 when he wrote his commentary on the Seс╣нaniс╣нk─Бrik─Б. I am, therefore, inclined to assign a period of about fifty years roughly from A.D. 1575 to A.D. 1625 to the literary activity of Harс╣гak─лrti.

Manuscript-material

The present edition of the ┼Ъ─Бrad─лy─Бkhyan─Бmam─Бl─Б is based on five manuscripts, four from the Government manuscripts Library at the Bhandarkar Oriental Research Institute, designated as BтВБ (=No. 1409 of 1887-91), BтВВ (= No. 281 of 1873-74), BтВГ(= No.1382 of 1884-87) and BтВД(No. 780 of 1875-76). The fifth manuscript designated as DтВБ belongs to the Deccan College Mss. Library. This manuscript being very corrupt had to be rejected after the 75th stanza of the second K─Бс╣Зс╕Нa. All the manuscripts are written in Devan─Бgar─л characters and with the exception of **B_(3,4)**are dated as follows:тАФ

BтВБтАУsaс╣Бvat 1760, BтВВтАУsaс╣Бvat 1792 and DтВБтАУsaс╣Бvat 1723. Unfortunately none of the five manuscripts utilized for this edition is complete and in some cases the readings had to be fixed with the help of the readings found in other lexicons.
